Political Turmoil Brewing in France 59

Parliament Opposes Salary Cuts and Tax Hikes

Pangou Government Faces Potential Collapse

Reuters, Paris, 15th - France is currently facing serious political turmoil triggered by the Finance Minister's proposed budget. The Finance Minister advocates cutting the salaries of cabinet members and officials, reducing government spending in various administrative departments, and increasing taxes. It is widely expected that this proposal will be strongly opposed by Parliament, and the Pangou government is facing the possibility of failure. Today, there are also rumors that a general strike of officials at all levels will occur to protest the salary cuts. The government held talks with representatives of officials at all levels today regarding the salary cuts, but the negotiations broke down, and the rumors intensified. The situation is indeed serious. However, calm observers believe that while the government may fail, a general strike is unlikely to materialize. Judging from the current situation, officials generally seem to want to resist the salary cuts in some way, but the method remains to be determined. There are three options currently available to civil servants: ㈠ A strike lasting several hours to show protest; ㈡ Adopting a policy of deliberate slowdown to backlog various official duties; ㈢ A general strike. Currently, the third option has not gained strong support, but no action is likely to be taken before Parliament votes on the supplementary budget.

National News Agency, Paris, 15th - Finance Minister Cheron's budget balancing plan, after being discussed by the cabinet all day, has been substantially passed today with slight revisions to the original plan. Regarding the reduction of official salaries and pensions, it has now been changed so that salaries below 12,000 francs will not be reduced, while those above this amount will be reduced in tiers, with larger salaries being reduced more. Furthermore, in order to please the Socialist Party, military spending has been reduced by 700 million francs. However, it remains unclear whether the crucial Socialist Party will be satisfied with this. Approximately after the government submits the temporary budget for February to Parliament on Tuesday, the party's attitude will become clear.

Philippine Independence Question 60

Stimson Writes Letter to Congress Explaining

House Still Maintains Original Plan After Deliberation

Philippine Assembly Rejects American Proposal

National News Agency, Washington, 15th - U.S. Secretary of State Stimson wrote a letter to Congress regarding the Philippine independence case, stating that U.S. possession of the Philippines creates a balance of power in the Far East. If abandoned immediately, it will lead to a chaotic trend in Far Eastern issues. This letter from Stimson was issued in support of President Hoover's position. At the time, Secretary of War Hurley, Secretary of Agriculture Hyde, and Secretary of Commerce Chaplin also sent letters to Congress, elaborating on the shortcomings of the Philippine independence letter. These letters were all published today. Stimson also stated in his letter that if the United States withdraws troops from the Philippines, it will have an unsettling effect on the political thought of various countries and Far Eastern nations and will affect the relationship between Far Eastern national political thought and the political thought of the rest of the world. Stimson also said that this case, on the one hand, disregards the distinction between individual freedom and self-governance for Filipinos, and on the other hand, ignores the difference between complete economic separation and political separation. Anyone who lives with Filipinos cannot help but be sure of their so-called desire for independence. The fundamental desire of the Filipinos is for a government with complete internal autonomy, and they still do not want to abandon U.S. protection and the benefits of the U.S.-Philippine union. Furthermore, this case is prone to misunderstanding and violates the plans of the founders of U.S.-Philippine policy. In short, the Philippine independence issue can only be resolved with fairness and impartiality, without any prejudice. The Filipinos' desire for self-governance should be fulfilled, but their interests should also be protected. Secretary of Agriculture Hyde said that American farmers have been deceived, and Secretary of Commerce Chaplin detailed the advantages and disadvantages of an independent Philippine government in terms of commercial relations. Secretary of War Hurley said that this case fails to protect the Philippines economically. Just considering sugar production, the Philippines will lose hundreds of millions of dollars annually after independence. Lin Bai Ke, advisor to the Chinese government, also said that he agrees with the U.S. President's veto of this case because it does not adequately protect the legal business operations of overseas Chinese in the Philippines. If this case is established, it is feared that the Filipinos will try to force overseas Chinese to become citizens, but he does not agree with the President's view that the Chinese people will constantly migrate to the Philippines, claiming that the Chinese people are interested in the Philippines for business, not agriculture, so only those engaged in business will want to go.

Reuters, Washington, 15th - Secretary of State Stimson and Secretary of War Hurley, on behalf of President Hoover, delivered a radio broadcast today regarding the Philippine independence issue. The Secretary of War stated that this case is economically unsound and could lead to war. The freedom granted by this case will ultimately have disastrous consequences. At a time when the stabilizing elements in the Far East are all being jeopardized, attention must be paid to the impact of this case on the Far East and the United States, and on moral dignity. The Philippine independence case was vetoed by Hoover on Friday, but the House of Representatives still maintained the original plan after deliberation that day.

Reuters, Manila, 16th - The Philippine House of Representatives held an informal meeting today and voted to decide on the Philippine independence proposal, even if the U.S. Senate overrides President Hoover's veto and passes it, it will not be accepted. It is expected that the Philippine Senate will also make the same decision. According to the proposal, the Philippines would enjoy freedom after ten years.

National News Agency, Manila, 16th - The Philippine independence case passed by the U.S. Senate and House of Representatives and vetoed by the President will be rejected by the Philippine Legislative Assembly. Today, a meeting of key members of the Philippine House of Representatives has decided to oppose the case. Senate President Quezon and other leaders of the independence movement attended the meeting to inquire about the attitude of the House of Representatives, saying that they will personally go to the United States, so they want to know the views of the Legislative Assembly on the case first. Therefore, the key members voted, and all but two advocated that if the case is sent to the Legislative Assembly, it will be rejected. The actions of the Philippine legislators are not unexpected. Quezon initially requested that if full independence is not granted immediately, then please U.S. Congress not to pass any proposals and telegraphed the United States, but the U.S. Congress did not pay attention and passed today's independence bill. The legislators in the United States firmly believed that this case would be accepted by the Filipinos, and the Filipinos initially seemed to express approval upon hearing the news of its passage, but after political leaders explained the various provisions within it, the number of opponents has been increasing daily. What the Filipinos oppose the most is the imposition of tariffs on Philippine goods before granting full independence and the implementation of immigration laws after independence. Some Filipinos who currently oppose independence say that the leaders of the independence movement, seeing the opposition, should take the opportunity to withdraw, and the enthusiasm for independence among the people has now slightly decreased.

Page 7

National Socialists Win Big in Lippe State Assembly Re-election 61

Reuters, Berlin, 16th - The Lippe state assembly elections were held today, and the National Socialist Party won a major victory. The National Socialist Party occupies nine seats and the Socialist Party occupies seven seats. It is expected that the results will strengthen the National Socialist Party's support for a parliamentary session to be extended to March.

National News Agency, Berlin, 16th - The National Socialist Party's victory in the Lippe state assembly elections has enabled it to increase its electorate from 5,500 to 38,800. It is expected that this will strengthen the party's opposition to the government. Chancellor Schleicher may dissolve parliament as a result of these elections. A notable point in the Lippe state elections is the substantial increase in votes for the Social Democratic Party, while the Communist Party and the German National People's Party lost a significant amount. The loss of the German National People's Party is particularly noteworthy, as it was rumored that Hugenberg had reached an agreement with Hitler to cooperate in Lippe to resist the Social Democratic Party.

National News Agency, Detmold, 15th - The Lippe state assembly elections are being held today. Although the state is only a small entity within the German Federation, the elections are being closely watched by the German people to gauge the rise and fall of the National Socialist Party's influence. Party leaders from Hitler downwards personally went to give speeches, reaching even remote villages. The intensity of the election campaign was rare. Therefore, the party has achieved its wishes in today's voting results, obtaining 38,000 votes, an increase of 5,500 votes compared to the Lippe state assembly elections in January 1929, and an increase compared to the total votes in the general election last November, but still a difference of 3,500 compared to the total votes of the party's heyday on July 30 last year. Although the National Socialist Party is the strongest party, it still cannot occupy a majority in the parliament and must unite with the German National People's Party and the German People's Party to form a government. Several conflicts occurred during today's election. In the small town of Brake, members of the Socialist Party and the National Socialist Party exchanged gunfire, injuring three of the former.

Germany Does Not Forget Militarism 62

Schleicher Emphasizes Conscription

Reuters, Berlin, 15th - German Chancellor Schleicher made astonishing remarks at a celebration of the 62nd anniversary of the founding of the German Empire held by the people of Berlin today, stating that the conscription system is the most important goal that Germany wants to achieve. The existence of Germany is due to the honorable achievements of the army. The symbol of German free men is the right to bear arms. Germany's enemies know that disarmament is enough to inflict a fatal blow on Germany. The German Chancellor also explicitly stated that Germany will not agree to any disarmament conference that disregards the principle of German sovereignty.

National News Agency, Berlin, 15th - The Joint Association of German WWI Veterans held its annual meeting here today, attended by German President Hindenburg, former German Crown Prince Wilhelm, General Mackensen, many cabinet members, and many former chiefs of staff of the German Imperial Army. Chancellor Schleicher, in his capacity as Minister of Defense, delivered a speech praising the honor of the former Imperial Army and the importance of national security. Schleicher's speech emphasized that after years of hard work, Germany has achieved equal status in the international community. Therefore, Germany will never sign any disarmament treaty that is not based on this principle of equality. Schleicher also repeatedly stated that Germany's sole aim and intention is to obtain the same guarantees as other countries. Schleicher concluded by saying that he has always supported the idea that citizens should have compulsory military education. This is not intended to expand the army, but to ensure that the people have the determination and preparation to defend the country in times of crisis.

Newspapers Record Frequent Disturbances

The stock exchanges in Madrid and Barcelona have been active, and the prices of national securities and industrial stocks are showing a thriving trend. All of this is sufficient to prove the increasing consolidation of Spanish internal affairs, and even if there are changes, there is no need to worry too much. The above is the government's point of view, but newspapers continue to publish facts of frequent disturbances in various places.

Wartime Scene in Qinhuangdao 64

Japanese Naval, Land, and Air Forces Provoke Us

Most Chinese and Foreign Shops Are Closed

The Whole Story of the Oomori Incident

Changli Correspondence, The reporter took the Beiping-Ning train from Changli to Qinhuangdao at 9:30 AM on the 11th for inspection. Along the way, stations such as Zhangjiazhuang, Liushouying, Beidaihe, and Nandaisi did not have a single passenger boarding. The area east of Changli to Qinhuangdao has become a war-torn zone, so there are only passengers fleeing west from Qinhuangdao, and very few passengers coming east from Changli. When the train arrived at Nandaisi station, sixteen li west of Qinhuangdao, one Japanese cruiser flagship, two destroyers, and two torpedo boats were seen moored on the sea. Black smoke swirled from the chimneys, and the gun covers had been removed, as if entering a major war. Two British warships were moored under Nanshan in Qinhuangdao, reportedly to protect British nationals and the Kailuan Mining Company, and the wharves. At 11:00 AM, the train arrived in Qinhuangdao. After the reporter got off the train, he visited Liu Zhenying, the battalion commander of the 9th Brigade who has been stationed there for a long time. At that time, Battalion Commander Liu was handling diplomacy, talking on the phone with Mr. Ceylon, the British station manager of the Qinhuangdao section. Later, it was learned that a Japanese military police officer named Oomori often traveled between Qinhuangdao and Shanhaiguan. The local people knew him well. At 1:00 PM on the 10th, Oomori suddenly wore a broken suit, covered with a broken green coat, and hid a pistol in his pocket. He walked from the Kailuan wharf south of the railway to the station, intending to spy on the true strength of our military preparations and to provoke us. When the passengers waiting for the train at the station saw Oomori, they cried out in alarm, saying that Japanese soldier Oomori had come. More and more people gathered around to watch. Seeing this, Oomori took out a pistol from his pocket and opened fire on the crowd, further enraging the crowd. The guards near the platform, fearing trouble, took Oomori back to the company headquarters and reported it to the company battalion commander for disposal. At 2:30 PM, Mr. Ceylon, the British station manager of the Qinhuangdao section of the Beiping-Ning Railway, came to negotiate. Oomori was taken away by Ceylon and returned to Japanese Navy Rear Admiral Tsuda, and the pistol he carried was also returned. Everyone thought that everything was fine, but on the morning of the 11th, Tsuda suddenly sent someone to make unreasonable demands: ㈠ Chinese soldiers at the station must be withdrawn immediately, and the guard rights must be handed over to the Japanese army; ㈡ Punish the perpetrators; ㈢ Compensate for the losses; ㈣ Guarantee that this will not happen again in the future; ㈤ Apologize to the Japanese side. For the sake of compromise, we have agreed to slightly withdraw the Chinese soldiers at the station, but the guard rights cannot be handed over to the Japanese army. The Japanese side is still not satisfied, and negotiations are underway. Currently, the scene in Qinhuangdao is that all large and small shops north of the railway have been closed. Only a few vendors selling fried dough sticks and pancakes walk in the face of the cold wind. South of the railway, because of the British merchants of the Kailuan Mining Wharf, there are also many foreign shops, and the order is still good, but 70-80% of them are also closed. The price of rickshaws is five times higher than usual. Japanese planes come to reconnaissance from time to time. Only the Kailuan Hotel was already full, and other hotels and apartments could not be found throughout Qinhuangdao, as they were all closed. Currently, the front line is still at Shihe, twenty-five li east of Qinhuangdao. According to people coming from near Shihe, the Japanese have not advanced further, only in the West Pass outside Shanhaiguan, three li away from the front line of our army in Shihe, but war is ultimately unavoidable. (January 12)

Northeastern Problem and the League of Nations (XIV) 65

Debate on the Afternoon of the 24th

(Both sides express their opinions twice) The Chairman said, according to precedent, when the Executive Yuan discusses reports of this nature, representatives from both sides of the dispute are given the opportunity to express their opinions twice. Therefore, aside from a very brief statement, this is the last opportunity for the Japanese representative to give a longer speech.

(Yosuke Matsuoka Sophisticates Again) Japanese Representative Yosuke Matsuoka said, "I am not very familiar with this practice. However, I am very grateful to the Chairman for giving me the opportunity to express some further opinions. Yesterday, I suggested that since the Chinese representative had made a serious accusation against a Japanese politician, he should provide evidence to substantiate his claim. This is my view. However, the Chinese representative not only did not provide evidence, not only did not admit that he had evidence, but instead presented a book written by me. The book is in Japanese, and the Chinese representative's citation seems to be accurate. This shows that the Chinese representative has agreed with my statement in the book that the Tanaka Memorial is a forgery. However, although I believe the Tanaka Memorial is a forgery, I have never designated anyone as the forger, nor have I said that the forger was a Chinese person. I only said that I had a report that the memorial was forged. I also did not specify a place name in the book. I remember when drafting it, I received reliable information that the memorial was forged jointly by a military attache of a certain country in Beiping and several Chinese people. After receiving this information, I did not believe it, because accepting such information should be done with extreme caution. Another piece of information said that the document was forged by a small number of irresponsible Japanese people. People who sell such forged documents exist in all countries of the world, not only in Japan. For the sake of clarity, please allow me to recount a small anecdote. Several years ago, we gathered in Tokyo to discuss proposals to be submitted to the Pacific Relations Conference. At that time, after the meeting, there were no results, and no plans were drawn up. Later, I learned from the most reliable source that a certain Japanese person had drafted a report, which contained a plan for the speeches that the Japanese representatives should make at the Tokyo conference. This report was purchased by the Chinese side for a huge sum of 50,000 yuan. This is a fact. I believe it to be true. Such behavior is done by lowly people in all countries, so there is nothing to be surprised about. However, the Chinese representative, in his responsible position, made an unsubstantiated accusation at the Executive Yuan, which is what I find most perplexing. My notes and speeches are all proven by facts. Regarding the Chinese representative's claim that the Chinese National Government did not fully guide the anti-Japanese economic boycott, I have already provided factual evidence to the contrary. At the same time, the Chinese representative also admitted that the Chinese government did participate in and encourage this movement to some extent. Now, I will present some more evidence as follows: First, the order of the Executive Yuan of the Nanjing National Government. The original text is in Chinese, and the translation can be found in Annex 230 of the investigation team's report, which contains instructions on methods to boycott Japanese residents and goods in China. Second, Instruction No. 9 of the Navigation Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Communications, addressed to the Tianjin Tokai Steamship Company. This company usually uses Chinese names, so the Chinese government mistakenly thought it was a Chinese enterprise and accidentally sent the secret order to a Japanese company. This is how we obtained this secret order. The content of the secret order can be found in Annex 232 of the investigation team's report. Third, the instructions of the Beiping Kuomintang Department regarding the economic boycott. The translation was sent by the Japanese representative to the investigation team for reference. All of the above can undoubtedly refute the Chinese representative's words. I urge the members of the Executive Yuan to examine it carefully. Also, regarding what the Chinese representative said this afternoon, I only need to point out one thing, that is, although the Chinese representative claimed that my speech avoided the main issues and focused on trivial issues, in fact, his speech was a self-portrait. If I turn to the right, the Chinese representative turns to my left. If I turn to the left, the Chinese representative turns to my right. This shows that the Chinese representative never dares to face me head-on. Regarding the Tanaka Memorial issue, I will not repeat it. Regarding the Sino-Russian Secret Treaty, the Chinese representative said that its purpose was to prevent Japanese aggression against Chinese territory. In fact, the members of the Executive Yuan only need to check the historical facts to understand who is right and who is wrong, and there is no need for me to repeat it. As for the telegram regarding the Northeastern Incident obtained by the Chinese representative, I really know nothing about it. I do not like to talk about what I do not know. Therefore, when necessary, I will pursue the facts of the incident, and perhaps I can present a visual account to you. The Chinese representative said that the main points of the Sino-Japanese dispute are: 1. Japanese military actions in Manchuria. Japan has already acquired Manchuria. Can this be called a self-defense action? 2. The "Manchukuo" independence movement. Is this movement truly based on the free will of the local people, as Japan claims? 3. The withdrawal of troops. Japan has not yet fulfilled this promise. 4. Japan promised not to aggravate the situation. Has Japan kept its promise? 5. Is there a peaceful solution to this problem? Regarding the above questions, the Japanese government's answer to the first and second questions is "yes," but the Chinese representative's answer is "no." Regarding the third and fourth questions, the Chinese representative's answer is also "no." Regarding the fifth point, I do not quite understand what the Chinese representative is saying, but I guess it roughly means that there are plenty of peaceful methods, which should be adopted by the League of Nations. Regarding all these points, we have clearly expressed Japan's views and position. Now, there is no need to say more, but if necessary, I will explain it to you in more detail next time. Finally, I dare to say that Japan has always been one of the most loyal member states of the League of Nations. This can be proven by facts and the actions of the Japanese government. However, China has never done anything until it has a complaint against Japan or another country, and then it uses this international peace organization to express its grievances. However, if future developments are absolutely incompatible with Japan's survival or Japan's policy of maintaining peace and order in East Asia, then the Japanese government still hopes to continue to be a loyal servant of the League of Nations."

(Chinese Representative's Written Response) The Chinese representative said that the Chinese side will answer the several points raised by the Japanese representative at the next meeting or in writing.

(Chairman and Matsuoka Debate on the Existence of the Investigation Team) "Chairman" I think there is no need to proceed with the discussion this afternoon. We will study the report tomorrow. Since the case we are discussing is so important, we should give the representatives of both China and Japan the opportunity to express their opinions within a reasonable scope. At the same time, we have already had a lot of success, so I hope that we can discuss the report again tomorrow afternoon.

"Matsuoka" I don't know what the Chairman's position is regarding the reservations I raised yesterday.

"Chairman" What the Japanese representative is referring to is the Executive Yuan's proposal to ask the investigation team to express whether they have changed their opinions. My observation on this matter is that, as a rule, before such an investigation team is dissolved, its chairman, representing the entire team, should attend the Executive Yuan meeting to explain the questions about the report to the members of the Executive Yuan. It seems that we should follow the usual practice this time as well.

"Matsuoka" If the questions asked by the Executive Yuan to the investigation team and the answers given by the investigation team are limited to the report itself, that is, the study of local facts, then I may accept this proposal. I deeply hope that the Chairman will give a clear explanation on this point.

"Chairman" My proposal last night was to ask the members of the investigation team to meet and consider whether the team has any intention to change any part of the report after hearing the opinions of the representatives of the two countries. Therefore, the meeting of the team should be based on the report and nothing else.

"Matsuoka" I object to this proposal. I believe that the investigation team no longer exists. If the Executive Yuan has a request, then the members of the investigation team may express their opinions and explain some events in the report and the points obtained by the team members during their local inspections. We can understand this point by examining the scope of the investigation team's duties. However, if the Executive Yuan and the investigation team are allowed to start asking each other questions about the China issue or the Manchuria issue, going beyond the report and the points obtained by the investigation team during their local inspections, and referring to the notes, opinions, statements, speeches, and everything else submitted by China and Japan in recent days, then I am afraid that I will be forced to ask many questions to each member of the investigation team. Once the questioning begins, the Japanese representative will have the right to ask questions about the report of the investigation team and its attachments, and even all the notes, opinions, statements, etc. This may not be completed in a week or a month. Can the members of the Executive Yuan not find it too long? This is why I object to this proposal.

"Chairman" The Japanese representative seems to have misunderstood. The only question that the investigation team should answer is whether they still hold the same opinions in their report after hearing the opinions of the representatives of China and Japan, or whether they intend to add or change some of their opinions. The investigation team must not specifically involve the opinions of the representatives of China and Japan, nor may they answer the objections expressed by both China and Japan.

"Matsuoka" I think I have not misunderstood the Chairman, but the Chairman seems to have misunderstood what I am advocating. Now, let us assume that the Chairman asks a question to the entire investigation team or individual members, and the investigation team or members express their opinions based on what has been discussed in recent days. Now, let us assume that the Japanese government cannot agree with this opinion. Then, we will naturally raise questions, asking the investigation team or individual members the reasons for reaching this opinion. Once the debate begins, it will take a long time. The Executive Yuan will not be able to deny its right to question until the Japanese government is satisfied. Now, let us assume that the entire investigation team or individual members declare to the Executive Yuan that although there have been debates between China and Japan in recent days, the opinions listed in the report of the investigation team have not changed. The Japanese representative will naturally have to ask questions about why this is so. Once the questioning begins, I am afraid that it will not be completed in a month.

"Chairman" I think that after the representative of the investigation team attends the Executive Yuan, the objections expressed by the Japanese representative will inevitably occur. Because the members of the Executive Yuan or the Chairman may ask the Chairman of the investigation team whether they intend to change their opinions. Since the Executive Yuan can ask the Chairman representing the team, it can naturally ask the entire investigation team the same question.

"Matsuoka" I think that regarding matters within the scope of the investigation team's report, such as the study of certain facts, it is okay to ask questions to the members of the investigation team. However, even if the members of the investigation team are invited to attend the Executive Yuan meeting, we do not need to ask them about what has been discussed at the Executive Yuan in recent days. In short, the questions and answers of the investigation team should be completely within the scope of their report. In addition, there is one more point that I would like to emphasize, that is, in the opinion of the Japanese government, the investigation team no longer exists after the report has been submitted. We have said this before. Therefore, the reason why we did not object when the investigation team was invited to attend the Executive Yuan meeting is because we tacitly agreed that the members of the investigation team should not participate in the Executive Yuan's considerations and proceedings. Therefore, we believe that although the Executive Yuan may ask individual members of the investigation team for their opinions, it may not ask the entire investigation team for their opinions, and may ask the team to explain the sections in the report and its attachments.

"Chairman" Regarding the point of whether the investigation team still exists, my opinion was expressed last night, that is, the investigation team still exists until it is formally dissolved by the Executive Yuan.

"Matsuoka" I object to this explanation. However, even if the investigation team still exists, it should not express opinions on the various considerations conducted within the Executive Yuan. In other words, the investigation team should not be regarded as having the right to attend the Executive Yuan to express opinions and judge right and wrong.

"Chairman" However, the Executive Yuan certainly wants to know all the opinions of the investigation team. The report of the investigation team was drafted before the representatives of China and Japan expressed their opinions. Therefore, there may be several points in these opinions that are sufficient to change the views of the investigation team. This is of course what the Executive Yuan is very willing to know. Regarding this point, I would like to ask other members of the Executive Yuan to express their opinions for reference.

(Czech Representative Upholds Justice) Czech Representative Benes said, "I fully agree with the Chairman's opinion on the procedural issue. According to precedent, investigation teams, etc., appointed by the Executive Yuan are invited to attend the Executive Yuan meetings so that the Chairman or members of the Executive Yuan can ask them to explain their opinions or ask them to answer questions about relevant matters. I think this practice is fully in line with the provisions of the League of Nations Charter regarding meeting procedures, and is not contrary to a kind of faithful sentiment towards the two parties in dispute before the Executive Yuan. Such events should be discussed openly. Therefore, in my opinion, the Chairman's proposal is fully in line with the spirit and precedent of the Executive Yuan. As for the question of whether the investigation team continues to exist, I think that what the report calls 'our work has now been completed' really means 'our work in the area has now been completed' and cannot be interpreted as the investigation team does not intend to answer questions before the Executive Yuan. Furthermore, the political plan formulated by the Executive Yuan should of course be formulated by the members of the Executive Yuan themselves. This is a matter of fact, not a matter of form. Because the investigation team of course cannot express political opinions, but the Chairman and members of the Executive Yuan have the right to seek explanations for the sections in the report at any time. Therefore, in my personal opinion, although there is currently no need for the investigation team to explain, I would very much like to have the opportunity to ask questions.

"Chairman" Are there any other members of the Executive Yuan who wish to express their opinions on this point?

"Matsuoka" Regarding this point, please give a clear and concise statement. The resolution passed by the Executive Yuan on December 10 last year, which appointed this investigation team, stated that "it was decided to appoint an investigation team of five people to go to the area for investigation and report to the Executive Yuan." My opinion is based on this section. Since the case before us is important, the provisions on the duties of the investigation team must be clearly recognized.

Guangdong Government Denies That the Commissioner in Hong Kong Signed Bills of Lading 66

Said to Violate the Regulations for Consular Visa of Foreign Bills of Lading

Guangzhou Communication: Since the Ministry of Finance established a resident visa commissioner in Hong Kong, the Southwest Political Affairs Council believes that this move violates the regulations for consular visa of foreign bills of lading, increases the burden on merchants, and raises prices. It specifically ordered the provincial government that goods using the visa commissioner's signed bills of lading in Hong Kong will not be allowed to be released. If the goods have already paid customs duties according to the usual practice and have not used the aforementioned signed bills of lading, they will be allowed to be released without any obstruction. After receiving the order, the provincial government issued an order to its subordinates yesterday, saying, "Now, we have received Instruction No. 2071 from the Southwest Political Affairs Committee of the National Government, stating that the 49th political affairs meeting of this committee was based on a report from the Chao Hai Customs Superintendent, approving the telegram from Wen Yingxing, the resident visa commissioner in Hong Kong, stating that the visa office was opened on the first of this month, and requesting that goods with the official bills of lading of this office be released, etc. The inspection of consular visa of bills of lading was previously notified by the Ministry of Finance and the Guangdong Provincial Government, and it has been reported to the Customs Service. Please check and issue orders to comply with the previous telegram, etc. This case was previously forwarded by the Executive Yuan to the consulates of the Republic of China abroad to issue regulations for consular visa of bills of lading, and amendments to the articles of the regulations were sent to the meeting, which was followed by the 28th political affairs meeting of this committee. The sections presented by the Chao Hai Customs Superintendent are not in accordance with the original regulations. 1. Article 2 of the regulations states that the consular visa of bills of lading referred to in the previous article can be obtained from the nearest consulate of the Republic of China. The goods must be clearly stated item by item, and signed by the person in charge, and sent to the Chinese consulate in the export location or a nearby export location for visa, etc. There is no provision for setting up a visa commissioner. 2. Article 1 of the regulations states that from the date of implementation of these regulations, all goods transported from overseas to China must be issued a bill of lading by the Chinese consulate. Goods transported from the interior of China through Hong Kong are not transported from overseas, and therefore do not need to be visa. 3. If the goods transported from overseas to China have already been visa by the Chinese consulate in the place, there is no need to visa again when passing through Hong Kong. 4. Although Article 5 of the regulations only stipulates that a handling fee of five customs gold units will be charged for each consular visa of bills of lading, since the regulations do not provide for the establishment of a commissioner, setting up a commissioner to charge fees outside the regulations will increase the burden on merchants. Based on the above reasons, it was decided to order the provincial government and the customs superintendents to continue to handle matters in accordance with the old regulations, without paying fees for signing, so as to facilitate merchants, and to order the customs superintendents not to release those signed by the commissioner. In addition to the separate orders, the provincial government shall immediately follow the instructions and implement them. Instruct囗囗to select capable personnel and jointly with 囗囗to send personnel to supervise the local military and police strictly. Goods that violate the order and use the bills of lading signed by the resident visa commissioner in Hong Kong shall not be released." (January 11)

Jiangsu Province Land Consolidation Plan 67

Divided into Two Types of Plans: Three Years and Five Years

To be Implemented After Review and Resolution

Zhenjiang Communication: The Jiangsu Province land consolidation program originally had a ten-year completion plan. The current concurrent director, Zhao Qilu, intends to shorten the completion year to five years or three years. The two plans he has proposed have been submitted to the Provincial Government Committee for review by the three departments of civil affairs, finance, and construction. Once approved, they will be submitted for resolution and announced for implementation. The original proposed consolidation plan is recorded as follows: "It is found that the land area of each county in Jiangsu Province is more than two to three million mu, with a total of 33 counties. There are 18 counties with more than one million mu, and 10 counties with less than one million mu. The total province is estimated to be more than 150 million mu. It is planned to actively consolidate from this year onwards, with a deadline for completion. The initial plan is for five years. A. Regarding topographic survey: 1. The provincial topographic survey is limited to the end of the 22nd year. The east-west and north-south three trunk lines will be completed uniformly, requiring an estimated expenditure of 160,000 yuan, which will be borne by the province. 2. The county topographic survey of each county will be completed uniformly by the end of the 23rd year, requiring a total expenditure of more than 460,000 yuan, which will be borne by each county. B. Regarding the clear measurement and registration: It is necessary to train personnel in advance. It is planned to hold the first phase in October of this year, graduating in four months, and then start the clear measurement of the 28 counties of the old Ning Zhen Chang Tong Su Song Tai. It will be completed by the end of the 24th year, requiring an estimated clear measurement fee of more than 8.6 million yuan and a registration fee of more than 560,000 yuan (registration will be handled immediately after the clear measurement of a city or township is completed). The second phase will continue in February of the 22nd year, graduating in four months, and then start the 20 counties of Huaiyang, completing by the 25th year, requiring an estimated clear measurement fee of more than 7.8 million.

Initiating the Organization of an Aviation Association 71

The Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association of this county, in view of the Japanese invaders' aggression against China, urgently needs to expand the anti-Japanese movement. (3) Appoint Qian Zhongliang, Chen Yixin, and Ma Zixin to draft the organizational outline of the Aviation Association and the organizational outline of the fundraising team for aviation to save the country. It is also heard that the amount of the fundraising for national salvation is set at 100,000 yuan to purchase an aircraft, named Wuxi. The fundraising method is that the county chamber of commerce is the captain, each trade association is the squad leader, the educational association is the captain, each school is the squad leader, each district chief is the captain, and each township chief is the squad leader, and they will conduct fundraising at any time. In addition, it is planned to solicit members, and the membership fee is divided into four types: A, B, C, and D. Type A members pay 5 yuan per year, paid in full at one time. Type B members pay 2 yuan. Type C members pay 5 jiao. Type D members (i.e., children's members) pay 2 jiao. Accumulate small amounts to make large amounts, and aircraft can be purchased. The 60 counties in Jiangsu Province, rich and poor, are connected to the two cities of Beijing and Shanghai, and at least 60 aircraft can be purchased. If it is extended to the whole country, military supplies such as artillery and anti-aircraft guns will not be lacking.

Requesting the Suspension of the Winter Grain Tax Surcharge by Telegram 72

The Wuxi County Party Department, the Chamber of Commerce, the Farmers' Association, the Educational Association, etc., believe that the price of rice has fallen, the rural economy has collapsed, and the people are extremely poor. They jointly telegraphed the provincial government, requesting the permission to suspend the winter grain tax surcharge to alleviate the people's hardship, and requesting the Jiangsu rice to be released to promote circulation, etc. Now, the reply telegram from the provincial government has been received, which reads, "It is found that the grain tax surcharge last year was due to the financial difficulties after the flood the year before, and the provincial treasury's income and expenditure were seriously insufficient. It was approved by the Ministry of Finance and forwarded to the Executive Yuan for approval to continue the extension for one year. As for the province's grain, it has now been allowed to be exported and circulated, and the value can be gradually increased. Please inform accordingly." The county party department has informed the various groups accordingly yesterday.

Local News

Mayor Wu Delivers Speech on Saving the Nation Through Aviation 79

Shanghai Citizens Deeply Affected by the January 28th Incident

Actively Engaging in Aviation Power and Air Equipment

Mayor Wu Tiecheng of this city delivered a speech at the city government's memorial week yesterday morning, saying, "Premier Sun Yat-sen's legacy of saving the nation through aviation should be most deeply recognized by the people today. The power and greatness of aviation has been very clearly and obviously revealed to us since the outbreak of the European War in 1914 up to the present day. Since the January 28th Incident last year, every citizen of Shanghai has personally experienced its threat. How should we engage in saving the nation through aviation after receiving this profound lesson? Since the European War, aviation technology and construction around the world have been developing day by day, and the fear of aerial terror is growing more and more profound. Therefore, countries are also intensifying their research into air defense. Our country not only has very little construction in aviation, but also pays little attention to and prepares for air defense equipment. If any country goes to war with China, the threat China will face can be easily imagined from the lessons learned last year. Compared to any country, China's current meager number of aircraft is practically zero. Even in terms of the speed of these meager aircraft, our country can only travel 120 miles per hour, while other countries have 180 to 200 miles per hour. In aerial combat, aircraft would only be for capture. However, under today's international situation, silently reflecting, the dangerous situation our country is in, the only way is to actively build national defense, concentrate all the intelligence, materials, and financial resources of the people of the whole country to achieve it. Only by building a solid national defense can we speak of self-defense. But according to the most urgent and relatively quick and easy thing to do in today's military, nothing is better than the air force. China is forced by the recent domestic and foreign situation, and the only way to quickly and actively engage in building aviation power and aerial equipment to strengthen national defense. The establishment of the China Aviation Salvation Association, its purpose is entirely at this point. The National Government recognizes saving the nation through aviation as the most critical plan, so it specially appointed domestic leaders as directors of the association to conduct widespread publicity throughout the country, and renamed it the China Aviation Association, which was established on New Year's Day this year. It has held several board meetings and is now actively preparing to start recruiting members. Colleagues of this government should know the importance of saving the nation through aviation. Now, when the association is soliciting members, it is planned to ask all the staff of this government to actively participate, to be an advocate for the entire city. The association's members are divided into five types: ordinary, special, sponsor, permanent, and group. Please determine each, and be sure to make the association a strong and effective non-governmental aviation organization to assist the government in building the air force to defend the country."

Female aviator Ms. Lin Pengxia, without avoiding the cold and hardship, personally went to the Northwest to investigate culture, politics, transportation, and air routes, in order to carry out on-the-spot development. Chairman Shao and the heads of various departments and divisions all hosted banquets to entertain me, and all sectors welcomed me with great enthusiasm. The whole city was shocked. At the provincial government meeting on New Year's Day, Chairman Shao personally invited me to speak. My ambition here is to develop the border regions and relieve the disaster victims. Therefore, there is no rice or wheat everywhere among the people. The natural disaster is severe, and there are also man-made disasters. Villages encountered by bandits are ruins, and the people have nowhere to return, so they mostly wander in the mountains and dare not return to their villages. The people are haggard and there is no life. The weather is now severely cold, and food prices are rising day by day. The disaster victims have reached the end of their ropes and have no way to survive. I cannot bear to witness the tragedy, so I will publicize this situation to all parties, and I hope that benevolent people will find ways to provide relief. I am sending seven tragic photos along the way, which will give you a glimpse. I have decided to sacrifice everything and do my best to rescue the suffering compatriots in the Northwest. Gentlemen, you are enthusiastic about loving the country, and you are willing to help me succeed."

Shanghai-Beiping Aviation Line to Fly North for the Second Time Today 85

Nie Kaiyi to Travel Together to Complete Unfinished Tasks

The China National Aviation Corporation's Shanghai-Beiping air route aircraft returned to Shanghai the day before yesterday. A reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency yesterday visited Nie Kaiyi, director of the airline's aircraft navigation section, and Li Diezhuang, secretary, to inquire about their feelings after the first voyage. According to their answer, the maiden voyage north was delayed to three days due to weather conditions. When heading south, it took off from Beiping at 7:40 AM and arrived in Longhua at 2:40 PM, traveling at 135 miles per hour. The speed of its flight was unexpected. The scheduled time for departure was 7:30 AM and arrival was 5:10 PM. According to the experience of the pilots, the wind direction is more suitable for flying between March and April, and the time can be further shortened. The mail carried southbound reached more than 100 kilograms, Qingdao more than 200 kilograms, and even Haizhou had 70 kilograms, which shows a glimpse of its development. Whether the number of flights will be increased to daily north and south departures will be determined after the second flight. Today at 7:30 AM, it is decided to go north as scheduled. It is driven by Chief Pilot An Lisheng, and Nie Kaiyi, director of the aircraft navigation section, will still travel together. Because the layout of the airports in Haizhou and Qingdao was not perfect due to the rush of the opening time, it is still necessary to build several necessary houses for rest and storage of gasoline and spare parts. The lease contract for the Tianjin airport has not yet been fully signed, and it is also urgent to complete it. Therefore, although Mr. Nie has already felt the hardship of traveling between Shanghai and Beiping last time, he still has to go north to guide and handle the above-mentioned matters.

Telegram of Victory from Yan Bowei's Troops 86

Fighting the Enemy in the Snow

The Office in Shanghai of the Commander of the Sixth Route Army of the Heat Resistance Against Japan received a telegram from Chaoyang yesterday, stating that Yan Bowei's troops, Wang Zhendong, learned that the Japanese army was gathering in Lingchao and attempting to invade Heat, so they coordinated with Jiang Peiran's army yesterday morning to launch a pincer attack on the Japanese army in Lingchao from the left and right wings. It happened to be snowing heavily this morning, and Wang and Jiang's troops all mustered their spirits and advanced through the snow. When they approached the Japanese army, they launched a fierce assault. Because the snowfall was too heavy, the Japanese army was unprepared, so they all abandoned their guns and fled in disarray. Wang and Jiang's troops were boosted and chased bravely. In this battle, more than 100 enemies were killed, more than 50 were injured, and 5 machine guns, 3 mortars, and more than 80 rifles were captured. The Japanese army has now retreated to Benniu Yingzi and Yuanjiagou.

Foreign Newspapers Praise Northern Postal Workers 95

Loyal to Their Duties Under Intense Bombardment

The Zilin News reports that it learned from reliable sources yesterday that the staff of the Chinese Northern Post Office were loyal to their duties and courageous in their work, often braving danger to maintain the details of the Yuguan Post Office. According to reports, since the outbreak of the war in Yuguan, the Post Office staff quickly found ways to restore postal traffic. At present, the post office at the station has been working daily from 9:00 AM to 3:00 PM, and a special place for selling stamps has been set up on the coast of Shanhaiguan to facilitate displaced overseas Chinese. All mail is delivered daily by pound, and all post office staff can work with peace of mind. No one wants to be afraid to leave their jobs until they receive orders. Bureau member Lu Haoming also went to the Japanese army to bomb the south gate, and under the fierce fire of 50 shells per minute, he automatically went to the area to rescue two colleagues who were suffering from illness. At present, the postal affairs in Yuguan District are presided over by a British youth, Darton. It is also heard that on the 4th of this month, a postman was transporting mail to Qinhuangdao, and after being blocked by the Japanese army on the way back, a Westerner named Kush, a customs officer, did not hesitate to take risks and walked from Shanhaiguan to Qinhuangdao to transport it on his behalf. His people are also righteous and courageous. Afterwards, the postal authorities quickly negotiated with the Japanese army to restore the office of the Chinese staff of the post office.

Reasons for Recent High Rice Prices 96

The Guowen News Agency reported yesterday that, according to people in the rice industry, the reasons for the recent surge in rice prices by about two yuan are quite noteworthy. It is heard that in the past, when grain was cheap, the villagers could not wait and sold their goods to seek wealth. Neighboring countries took advantage of our cheap grain and made unscrupulous merchants try to petition the government for grain transport passports, ostensibly to transport grain to Qingdao, Jinan, and other places, but secretly to smuggle it abroad, resulting in a continuous rise in rice prices in recent days, and there is a tendency for it to continue to increase. If it is not stopped in time, I am afraid that there will be insufficient green and yellow in the future. Those who sell their goods to seek wealth today will buy them back at several times the price in the future, and their economic ability will be even more unable to bear it. This is a serious step today, which is enough to create social unrest in the future. Shouldn't the authorities pay close attention to it?

There Is Another Bizarre Electronic Sound of the Missing Yu Long Vessel 97

Between Hong Kong and Hainan Island in Three Days

Insurance Company Asks About the Truth in a Letter

Relief to Family Members of Crew Members First

After the missing Yu Long vessel, which was represented by the Tongyu Shipping Company, the company yesterday sent a letter to the Jianghai Customs to forward it to the customs of various ports for investigation. The families of the crew members will be given advances on their wages to comfort them. There are still vessels passing between Hong Kong and Qiongzhou Island that have received radio transmissions from the Yu Long vessel. The bizarreness of the incident is unprecedented. The details are as follows.

History of Yu Long 98

The Yu Long vessel has a deadweight tonnage of 2,700 tons and a net cargo tonnage of 2,400 tons. It was manufactured in the United Kingdom in 1892 and purchased by a Norwegian merchant of the Yu Long Shipping Company, valued at 100,000 taels. It is represented by the Tongyu Shipping Company. The shipowner is Norwegian, Yal Sheng, the chief mate is Xu Shanming, and the chief mechanic is Qi Xinyu. This time, it was repaired in Shanghai and a new furnace was installed. At the end of November, it sailed from Shanghai to Hongji in Annam to load Hongji coal. It went missing after sailing out of Hongji on December 8.

Bizarre Track 99

The company entrusted the International Radio Station of the Ministry of Communications to forward it to the Yu Long vessel by radio, but there was no response. The Hong Kong Radio Station is now continuing to search for it by radio. On the 2nd of this month, the Yingping vessel of the Yingping Company received a radio transmission from the Yu Long vessel between Hong Kong and Hainan Island, reporting only the name of the vessel, and then it was cut off. On the 3rd of this month, the Fengxiang vessel of the Yongping Company also received a radio transmission from Yu Long, reporting only the name of the vessel, which was the same as the Yingping vessel. Therefore, after the company received the notification, it felt that the incident was bizarre and could not guess the truth.

Customs Investigation 100

The Tongyu Company, based on the ship names connected by the telegrams from Yingping and other vessels, predicted that the vessel may not have sunk. Yesterday, it sent a special letter to the Shanghai Jianghai Customs, asking it to forward it to ports such as Xiamen, Hong Kong, Guangdong, Shantou, and Kowloon to investigate the traces of the Yu Long vessel.

Previously Insured 101

A reporter from Xinsheng News Agency met with the company's accountant yesterday, who said that the purchase price of the Yu Long vessel was 100,000 taels, and it was insured by three companies, Zhaotai, Huaan, and Lianbao, totaling 50,000 taels. The Hongji coal it loaded was worth about 30,000 yuan. Yesterday, the Zhaolong and other insurance companies all sent letters inquiring about the truth.

Relief to Family Members 102

The entire crew of the vessel is about 40 people. The families of the crew members continued to go to the company at 9:00 AM yesterday to plead for relief. Chen Yisheng, the manager of the company, in view of the suffering of the families, gave each person an advance on their salary for one and a half months yesterday to provide relief. After receiving the money at 12:00 AM, the families of the crew members dispersed.

The New Director of the Savings and Remittance Bureau, Tang Baoshu, Assumed Office Yesterday Morning 103

Li Jingcong from the Ministry of Communications Presided over the Oath Ceremony

Mr. Tang Baoshu, the newly appointed director of the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, arrived at the bureau yesterday and took his oath of office. Li Jingcong, the Director of General Affairs from the Ministry of Communications, was specially appointed to preside over the oath ceremony. Zhang Xincheng, the Chief Accountant, and Lu Rongguang, the Section Chief, were appointed to supervise the handover of records. Details are recorded as follows:

(Circumstances of Taking Office) Director Tang arrived at the bureau at approximately 9:00 AM yesterday. The former director, Yang Jianping, handed over all important documents one by one. Zhang Xincheng and Chen Rongguang, both appointed by the Ministry of Communications, supervised the handover. The handover was completed at approximately 10:00 AM. Director Tang then immediately convened all staff members to hold the oath ceremony. Li Jingcong, the Director of General Affairs from the Ministry of Communications, represented the Ministry to preside over the oath ceremony and delivered a speech, hoping that Director Tang would: 1) strictly supervise the use of savings, 2) develop the bureau's operations to become professional. Director Tang then delivered a reply and the meeting adjourned. Among those who came to offer congratulations were Huang Naishu, the Director of the Postal Administration; Chen Xing, the President of the Central Bank; Dai Enqi, the General Manager of China National Aviation Corporation; and Yang Dunfu, Tang Baohuang, Tang Baotai, Chen Gongzhe, Ang Ge, and many others.

(Public Statement) Director Tang made a public statement to reporters from various newspapers yesterday, saying, "I have been appointed by the government to serve as the Director of the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau. At the beginning of my tenure, everything is still under review, and I dare not comment too much. However, the savings and remittance business has a significant impact on the national economy. The Ministry of Communications is currently studying the system and drafting organizational regulations. I have been ordered to take over, and I can only strive to promote the development of the bureau and ensure the safety of savings. As for personnel administration, I will be impartial and strive for the professionalization of duties. I hope that all sectors will provide guidance and jointly promote the advancement of state-owned enterprises. This is what I most hope for and am willing to accept sincerely."

(Tang's Biography) Tang Baoshu is 42 years old, from Zhongshan, Guangdong. He studied finance and economics at the University of Berlin in Germany, earning a master's degree. He spent many years in Europe and the United States, studying industrial and commercial conditions. After returning to China, he served as the president of the Hong Kong National Commercial Savings Bank for more than ten years. He has extensive experience in banking and is very familiar with financial situations.

Changes to the Road System in Zhabei 104

Draft Plan Released Yesterday

Since the January 28th Incident, all residential buildings and roads in Zhabei, Shanghai, have been almost completely destroyed. Recently, the Ministry of Railways decided to relocate the North Railway Station, so the municipal government believes that the original road system needs to be changed. The Public Works Bureau first drafted a plan for the changed road system and submitted it to the municipal government. The 216th municipal meeting approved it and sent it to the Ministry of Railways for review. It is learned that the Ministry of Railways has handed it over to road experts for review and found it usable. Therefore, it replied to the municipal government the day before yesterday. The municipal government officially announced the plan yesterday. The plan stipulates that the Jiaotong Road, which starts from Baoshan Road in the east and ends at Datong Road in the west, and the newly built January 28th Road, each have a width of 18.3 meters. The Jiaotong Road west of Datong Road has a width of 20 meters.

News from the Institute of Social Sciences of the Academia Sinica 108

The Institute of Social Sciences of the National Academia Sinica is one of the research institutions of the Academia Sinica. It was established at the end of 1927 and has been in existence for five years. In previous years, due to the lack of a fixed address, it moved between Beijing and Shanghai several times. It was not until the spring of last year that a new site was determined on the southeast side of Qintian Mountain in Nanjing. Construction was completed at the end of the year. All departments of the institute moved in from Shanghai one after another this spring. The director of the institute was originally concurrently held by the president of the Academia Sinica, Cai Yuanpei. Recently, President Cai has been busy with affairs and has appointed Yang Xingfo, the director-general of the Academia Sinica, to concurrently serve as director. The latest news from the institute is summarized below: 1) Facilities: The institute's building is a steel-and-concrete convex-shaped building located on the southeast side of Qintian Mountain in Nanjing, in front of Jiming Temple. The environment is quiet and the scenery is excellent, making it a good place for retreat and cultivation. It has a library with three floors, which can hold 100,000 volumes. The library's books are mainly in the social sciences. Over the years, it has been actively collecting books. As of the end of June of this year, it has reached 65,735 volumes, including 27,497 volumes of Chinese and Japanese books, 11,086 volumes of Western books, 16,746 volumes of Chinese and Japanese magazines and gazettes, and 10,406 volumes of Western magazines and gazettes. In addition, there are many instruments and specimens, including 11 kinds of anthropometric instruments for ethnology, 3 kinds of cameras, a magic lantern, more than 100 ethnic films, more than 700 ethnic specimens, and hundreds of charts and photographs. Last winter, in order to collect local chronicles from all over China, a large-scale solicitation was sent to local governments in various provinces, cities, and counties across the country. About 300 books were sent in response from various places. Together with the original local chronicles, there are more than 700 books. In order to strive for completeness, it is planned to send a second letter of solicitation, which is already in progress. Opening of the library: Since the institute moved to Nanjing, due to its rich collection of books, many staff members of various institutions and university professors in Nanjing have requested to visit the library to read books. In order to meet the needs of the outside world, regulations for borrowing books for visitors have been formulated and will soon be available for public reading. 2) Research work: In addition to the results that have been made into reports and published, which can be found in the catalog of the Academia Sinica's publications, the current research in progress or reports that have been written but not yet published can be divided into four subjects: ethnology, sociology, economics, and legal studies, which are listed as follows: (A) In ethnology, there are comparative studies of the use of knotted ropes for record-keeping and primitive writing by various ethnic groups in the world (researcher: Cai Yuanpei), research on the Hezhen ethnic group in the lower reaches of the Songhua River (researcher: Ling Chunsheng), a survey of the Li people on Hainan Island (researcher: Shi Tubo), Chinese translation of foreign ethnic names (researcher: Rui Ruiyifu), and compilation and translation of ethnographic survey methods (compilers: Ling Chunsheng, Zhang Qisun), etc. (B) In sociology, there are surveys of the rural economy in Wuxi (researchers: Chen Hansheng, et al.), surveys of the rural economy in Baoding (researchers: this institute cooperated with the Beiping Social Survey Institute), surveys of the transfer of Baoshan's produce (researchers: Chen Hansheng, et al.), surveys of the contract labor system in Shanghai factories (researchers: Chen Hansheng, et al.), and surveys of the rural economy along the railway (researchers: Chen Hansheng, et al.). (C) In economics, there are studies on China's international trade statistics (researchers: Hu Jichang, et al.), surveys of import and export cargo miscellaneous fees in Shanghai's foreign trade (researchers: Fan Mingmao, et al.), and studies on labor insurance (researchers: Luo Zhiru, et al.). (D) In legal studies, there are studies on the Shanghai International Settlement system (researchers: Xu Gongsu, et al.), studies on concession areas (researchers: Qiu Jinzhang), studies on international law in the Shanghai Incident (researchers: Wang Dehui, et al.), and studies on treaty revision (researchers: Wang Dehui).

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Takeover of the Yangtze Wharf Issue 116

Should Be Resolved Within This Month

Yang Zhixiong, the managing director of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, told a reporter from the Central News Agency yesterday that the issue of the company taking over the Yangtze Wharf should be resolved within this month. The wharf was leased to the Haiyang Company by the previous director. The land of the wharf belongs to the company, while the warehouses belong to German merchants. After the expiration, it has been recovered by the Ministry of Communications. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company hopes to manage the wharf to develop shipping. Moreover, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company is a state-owned enterprise, so there is no problem. However, in order for the company to take over, it must repay the 240,000 taels advanced by the Ministry of Communications when it recovered the wharf. It is currently negotiating with the Ministry of Communications whether the transfer will be made by transferring accounts between the two parties or by paying in cash, which is only a procedural matter. The Yangtze Wharf is close to the Central Wharf. In the future, after the company takes over the construction of warehouses and deepens the waterway, the wharf business can be expected to develop.

Henan Deng County Suffers a Severe Disaster and Begs for Relief 117

The China Jisheng Association recently received a report from Deng County, stating that Deng County is located in the extreme southwest border of Henan Province and has long been a den of bandits. Villages in the western half have been reduced to ruins and overgrown with weeds. There are more than 8,000 hectares of uncultivated land. The people have long been unable to make a living. Last summer, all rivers overflowed and torrential rains continued for 57 days. The autumn harvest failed completely. Subsequently, epidemics broke out and tens of thousands died. Droughts ravaged the area and sowing was disrupted. The wheat season this year only yielded 20%. Between summer and autumn, there was no rain in the northwest of the county for several months, and there was no autumn harvest at all. Although some areas in the southeast were slightly moistened by rain, the harvest was not even 30%. A small number of wheat and beans were sown, but gradually withered. In addition, large groups of roving bandits such as Zhang Laoliu, Wei Guozhu, and Wang Tai ravaged the area, and tens of thousands of communist bandits led by Xu Xiangqian disturbed the area. All kinds of disasters have been experienced, and the households are empty. The burden on the people of Deng is very heavy, and the plight is unimaginable. Currently, people in the north of the county are dismantling houses for those who transport and sell them in counties such as Neixiang and Zhenping. Villagers in various districts and townships are asking the districts for relief, and those who flee to beg for food are endless. In each township, there are households that cannot obtain a single meal all day long. Everywhere you look, there are old and young men and women, crying out in hunger, which is unbearable to hear. The state of waiting for death is unbearable to see. Starving people are often seen. In this severe winter, how can there be any survivors? The public earnestly requests your association to have pity on the special disasters and sufferings of Deng County, which are not found in other counties, and quickly allocate huge sums of money to provide relief. The association is currently receiving letters and documents reporting tragic disasters, which are pouring in like snowflakes and cannot be dealt with. It is hoped that charitable comrades at home and abroad will have compassion for this catastrophe, make a vow to save people, and create immeasurable blessings.

Ningbo Fellow Countrymen's Association Resolves Opinions on Clearing Sand Fields 118

Telegram to the Chairman of Zhejiang Province

The Ningbo Fellow Countrymen's Association in Shanghai believes that the former Ningchen Sand Field Branch violated the regulations of the Ministry and disposed of privately-owned sand fields without authorization, causing disputes. Yesterday, it telegraphed the Zhejiang Provincial Government to state its opinions on the resolution. The telegram read, "To Chairman Lu of the Zhejiang Provincial Government in Hangzhou, we have received a copy of the proposed methods for clearing sand fields, making up for deficiencies, and resolving issues issued by the Department of Civil Affairs. After inviting fellow countrymen to the association to view it, everyone believed that the proposed methods of the Department of Civil Affairs excessively focused on facts and did not effectively correct the failure of the former Ning County Sand Field Branch to comply with the regulations of the Ministry, causing all kinds of disputes. Now, after discussion by the association, the following opinions are put forward: 1) All regulations and detailed rules of the Ministry's order for Zhejiang Province to clear sand fields must be strictly followed by the county bureaus in the future and shall not be invoked with specially approved cases, so that the people have nowhere to turn. 2) The scope of handling sand fields should still strictly follow the regulations of the Ministry, and the procedures for the county bureau should be followed. 3) All cases that have been sold by tender should be declared invalid because the branch did not implement the statutory procedures. Therefore, we telegraphed the chairman for your assessment, vigorously presided over the matter, to emphasize merit and prevent disputes."

Resolution of Dispute at Zhenfeng Cloth Factory 120

Three Resolution Methods Signed

According to Dagongshe, regarding the labor unrest at Zhenfeng Cloth Factory on Beijing-Jiangxi Road, Zhabei, the Bureau of Social Affairs convened both parties again at 2:00 PM yesterday for mediation. The labor representatives were Xue Qisen and Zhong Xiaobao, the capital representatives were Sun Zhihong and Wei Zhuan, and the Municipal Party Headquarters representative was Fan Guoren. Zhu Jintao, Chairman of the Third Section of the Bureau of Social Affairs, declared that the case had been repeatedly mediated, but no results had been achieved due to the insistence of both parties. He hoped that both parties would make concessions to avoid prolonging the dispute. Negotiations then began, and the parties agreed to the following three solutions, which were announced for resolution: 1. Wages will be maintained at the current level. 2. Starting in February, the system of quick rewards and slow punishments will be restored. 3. The capital will be allowed to suspend work for ten days for internal reorganization, and during the suspension period, a meal allowance of two yuan will be issued.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Initiates the Establishment of a Joint Chamber of Commerce Office 121

Unite and Rise Up to Resist Foreign Aggression Together

In view of the increasingly urgent foreign aggression and the unpredictable changes in the current situation, the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce believes that all merchants should unite and rise up to respond, and has initiated the organization of a joint Chamber of Commerce office. Telegrams were sent to Chambers of Commerce in various regions, requesting them to send representatives to Shanghai to discuss implementation methods. The original telegram is recorded below: To the Chambers of Commerce in Nanjing, Beiping, Tianjin, Jinan, Xuzhou, Zhengzhou, and Hankou: The current situation is changing, and commerce is declining. All of us merchants should have the necessity to unite and rise up. It is planned to organize a joint Chamber of Commerce office in Shanghai to respond to the situation. We hope that each Chamber will send one to three representatives to Shanghai to discuss the matter. We look forward to your telegraphic reply. Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce Seal.

Director Huang Rectifies Passenger Transportation on Two Railways 122

The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways have more than 45,000 passengers traveling daily. Passenger transport has always been the largest source of income for the railways. Since taking office, Director Huang Boqiao has realized that the waterways of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces are convenient for transportation, and competition is extremely fierce. He is deeply concerned that if the management and response are slightly inappropriate, passengers will abandon the railways for ships, affecting passenger transport. It is reported that he has ordered the Traffic Department and the Police Department to pay special attention and supervise their subordinates. All station staff and railway police who have daily contact with passengers should do their best, sincerely and humbly, to provide convenience for passengers at all times and places. They must answer inquiries in detail, take good care of requests, accept arguments with moderation, and provide assistance in times of danger. It is forbidden to show arrogance or anger, use rude words or harsh voices, so that passengers do not see the two railways as a fearful journey, regard them as bureaucratic, and tarnish the reputation of the railways. He has also secretly sent officers to conduct strict inspections at any time. Furthermore, the number of passengers in third and fourth-class carriages on the two railways is the largest, but the crowding of seats, the simplicity of equipment, the lack of attention to cleanliness, and the lack of uniformity in appearance are most prominent in third and fourth-class carriages, which inevitably causes passenger complaints. It is reported that Director Huang ordered the Traffic and Mechanical Departments yesterday to discuss a plan and find ways to rectify the situation, so that passengers will feel comfortable and convenient, thoroughly develop the spirit of commercialization and popularization, and achieve the mission of the two railways as a state-owned transportation enterprise.

Old Woman Fatally Injured by a Large Wooden Box 123

Madam Zhu, mother of Jie Jianyuan from Gaoyou, who was nearly sixty years old, returned to her hometown the day before yesterday and boarded a Datong Company steamer in Nanshi. Unexpectedly, while unloading cargo, a huge wooden box fell and crushed her right leg, fracturing and shattering the leg bone. She was sent to Xin Puyu Hall for treatment, but it was ineffective, and she died yesterday. Jie Jianyuan was notified and petitioned the Local Court to request an autopsy and investigation.
