Facial Expressions Difficult on the Screen 258

— Huaming

The directors of Hollywood pay close attention to the every move of the actors, because every actor has a habitual action and unnatural expression, which are often revealed unintentionally. When the director encounters this situation, he immediately corrects it, and sometimes even scolds them face-to-face, never ignoring it.

Norma Shearer has a talk about this. She said: "Almost everyone has habitual actions, which they don't feel themselves, but others find very annoying. My worst habitual action is often turning my head back. At first, I didn't feel anything, and some people said that this posture of mine was very beautiful. Later, I turned my head back non-stop, and I myself felt very ugly. From then on, every time I wanted to turn my head back, I immediately stopped myself, and this bad habit gradually disappeared."

The most difficult expression is smiling. Norma's chuckles and giggles in the film The Divorcee are completely natural and not forced at all. This is because she practiced hard, so to perform an expression, she can do whatever she wants. Frank Borzage, the director of Seventh Heaven, said: "I pay the most attention to the natural and calm expression. Whenever there is a forced movement, I will reform it. The actors who perform with me have the same view as me, so the films I direct do not have cramped expressions."

Now, let's briefly record the habitual actions of several stars:

RKO's new female star, Katharine Hepburn, often tightens her lips, making her lips wrinkled.

Glenda Farrell likes to raise her hand and put her little finger on her teeth, and she raised it three times in one scene in the film I Am a Fugitive.

Constance Bennett always raises her hand to touch her hair in every play, as if she feels that her hair is messy, and she must touch it before she feels at ease.

Mary Pickford's bad habit is often pouting her lips, but she hasn't been seen pouting her lips for a long time.

Myrna Loy's squint in the two films "Rescue Girl" and "Emma Hates History" is that she should have this expression in these two films, but she squints too much, so it is inevitable that it feels tasteless.

Joan Crawford always lowers her head before looking at a person, but she has now changed it.

Irene Dunne's breathing becomes rapid before she opens her mouth to speak.

Marion Davies often blinks her eyes when filming.

The above are all innate habits, which are not easy to change for a while, but must be changed.

The Story of the "Match King" ⑽㈠ 259

— Translated by Ximeng

After a while, the long-distance call was connected.

"Hello, hello," Eric shouted loudly. "Yes, I'm Eric, eh, Paul, the loan from Barclays Bank!"

Before he could finish speaking, Paul interrupted:

"Eric, write it down, this is extremely important. Quickly find out which place near the North Sea produces the best Periwinkles. Once you find it, use ice and hire a plane to send it here. I must have it by noon tomorrow. What?" He obviously heard that Eric wanted to report on many official matters and was a little impatient. "You can arrange it as you like, don't be busy, don't worry, I will find a way. Goodbye."

"But, Paul! Barclays!" Eric's face turned green with anxiety, but the phone on the other side had already hung up. He said to the many people around him who were stunned, "He hung up the phone."

He had no other choice but to reschedule the board meeting. He hurriedly hired a plane to prepare to go to Salzburg himself. But he didn't dare to disobey Paul's order, so he first had to find Periwinkles.

Eric flew to Salzburg tomorrow afternoon with the Periwinkles found in the North Sea, and tried his best to talk to Paul about serious business. Finally, Paul agreed to return to Stockholm with Eric.

"We don't need to say goodbye," Paul said to Mouna! She came to the airfield to see him off in person. "I'll be back here on Tuesday, and then we'll "go to Mirabell.""

"Mirabell! Tuesday," Mouna nodded carefully. "I'll wait for you, will you really come back?"

"What in the world can hold me back?" Paul whispered to Mouna.

"My dear!" Mouna said softly. "I'll wait until Tuesday, thank you, thank you for the Periwinkles, thank you for everything, you're really lovely."

But on Tuesday, Mouna waited for Paul to come, but he didn't come, and she sat alone in the bedroom, listless.

The board meetings were endless, and all kinds of important matters had to be handled by Paul Kruger himself with his superior intelligence and cunning, and others could not do it. But in the end, he actually borrowed a surprising amount of money from the Swedish National Bank. He went to the office and showed the loan contract to Eric.

"Isn't this the loan from Barclays Bank settled," he said, then slumped back in his chair. "My power can save Germany, and it can save France, I can save Europe, and other continents, but!" As he said this, his eyes stared at Mouna's beautiful photo. "I can't save myself!" His thoughts were obviously turning to Salzburg.
